<p><b>Rockchip</b> (Fuzhou Rockchip Electronics Co., Ltd.) is a Chinese <a href="/wiki/Fabless_manufacturing" title="Fabless manufacturing">fabless</a> <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor_industry" title="Semiconductor industry">semiconductor</a> company based in <a href="/wiki/Fuzhou" title="Fuzhou">Fuzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> province. It designs <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System_on_a_Chip" title="System on a Chip">SoCs</a> using licensed <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor_intellectual_property_core" title="Semiconductor intellectual property core">SIP cores</a> from other companies. Due to its evolution from the MP3/MP4 player market, most Rockchip SoCs feature advanced media decoding logic but lack integrated <a href="/wiki/Baseband_processor" title="Baseband processor">cellular radio basebands</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Rockchip is a leading supplier of SoC solutions to Chinese white-box tablet manufacturers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014-05-24_DigiTimes_article_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014-05-24_DigiTimes_article-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TechNews_market_share_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-TechNews_market_share-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DigiTimes_Q2_2014_market_share_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-DigiTimes_Q2_2014_market_share-6">[6]</a></sup> as well as supplying OEMs such as <a href="/wiki/Asus" title="Asus">Asus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asus_MemoPad_8_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asus_MemoPad_8-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asus_MemoPad_10_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asus_MemoPad_10-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">HP</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HP_Slate_7_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-HP_Slate_7-9">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toshiba_Excite_7_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toshiba_Excite_7-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toshiba_Excite_7c_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toshiba_Excite_7c-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rockchip is an <a href="/wiki/ARM_Holdings" title="ARM Holdings">ARM</a> licensee and uses the <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM architecture</a> for the majority of its projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, on 27 May 2014 <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> announced that it has entered into a strategic agreement with Rockchip to accelerate the adoption of the Intel architecture and Intel's communication-based solutions for a range of entry-level tablets targeted at the worldwide market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_announcement_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_announcement-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Markets_and_competition">Markets and competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Markets and competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the market for SoC solutions for tablets, Rockchip faces competition from <a href="/wiki/Allwinner_Technology" title="Allwinner Technology">Allwinner Technology</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MediaTek" title="MediaTek">MediaTek</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TechNews_market_share_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-TechNews_market_share-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_Motley_Fool_article_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_Motley_Fool_article-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Actions_Semiconductor" title="Actions Semiconductor">Actions Semiconductor</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spreadtrum" title="Spreadtrum">Spreadtrum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leadcore_Technology" title="Leadcore Technology">Leadcore Technology</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsung_Semiconductor" title="Samsung Semiconductor">Samsung Semiconductor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Broadcom" title="Broadcom">Broadcom</a>, <a href="/wiki/VIA_Technologies" title="VIA Technologies">VIA Technologies</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article-13">[13]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Amlogic" title="Amlogic">Amlogic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>After establishing a leading position early in the developing Chinese tablet SoC market, in 2012 it faced a challenge by Allwinner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EETimes_2012_Rockchip_article_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-EETimes_2012_Rockchip_article-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2012, Rockchip shipped 10.5 million tablet processors, compared to 27.5 million for Allwinner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-EETimes_2013_Allwinner_article-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, Rockchip subsequently improved its competitive position. For Q3 2013, Rockchip was forecast to ship 6 million tablet-use application processors in China, compared to 7 million for Allwinner who mainly shipped single-core solutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Rockchip was reported to be the number one supplier of tablet-use application processors in China in Q4 2013, Q1 2014 and Q2 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014-05-24_DigiTimes_article_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014-05-24_DigiTimes_article-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DigiTimes_Q2_2014_market_share_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-DigiTimes_Q2_2014_market_share-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chinese SoC suppliers that do not have <a href="/wiki/Baseband" title="Baseband">cellular baseband</a> technology are at a disadvantage compared to companies such as MediaTek that also supply the <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> market as white-box tablet makers increasingly add phone or cellular data functionality to their products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Intel Corporation has made significant investments into becoming a player in the tablet processor market and was heavily subsidizing its entry into the low-cost tablet market as of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_Motley_Fool_article_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_Motley_Fool_article-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_with_Intel">Cooperation with Intel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cooperation with Intel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2014, <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> announced a strategic agreement with Rockchip to jointly deliver an Intel-branded mobile SoC platform based on Intel's <a href="/wiki/Atom_(system_on_chip)" title="Atom (system on chip)">Atom</a> processor and <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> modem technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_announcement_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_announcement-3">[3]</a></sup> Under the terms of the agreement, the two companies will deliver an Intel-branded mobile SoC platform. The quad-core platform will be based on an Intel Atom processor core integrated with Intel's 3G modem technology, and is expected to be available in the first half of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_announcement_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_announcement-3">[3]</a></sup> Both Intel and Rockchip will sell the new part to OEMs and ODMs, primarily into each company's existing customer base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intel_announcement_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-Intel_announcement-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of October 2014, Rockchip was already offering a low-end <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> solution, Intel's XMM 6321, through its customer base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> It is a two chip solution consisting of a dual-core application processor (either with Intel processor cores or ARM Cortex-A5 cores) with integrated modem (XG632) and an integrated RF chip (AG620) that originates from the cellular chip division of <a href="/wiki/Infineon_Technologies" title="Infineon Technologies">Infineon</a> (which Intel acquired some time ago). The application processor may also originate from Infineon or Intel. Rockchip has not earlier targeted the smartphone space in a material way.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Products">Early Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early Products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>RK26xx series</b> - Released 2006.</p>
<p><b>RK27xx series</b> - Rockchip was first known for their RK 27xx series that was very efficient at <a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a>/MP4 decoding and was integrated in many low-cost <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_digital_media_player" title="Mobile digital media player">personal media player (PMP)</a> products.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK28xx_series">RK28xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: RK28xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>RK2806</b> was targeted at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_digital_media_player" title="Mobile digital media player">PMPs</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARM9" title="ARM9">ARM9</a>26EJC 600 MHz CPU + DSP Core</li>
<li>SD, DDR RAM support</li>
<li>Up to 1280×720 H.263 and H.264 software video acceleration.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RTOS" title="RTOS">RTOS</a> support</li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK2808A</b> is an ARM926EJ-S derivative. Along with the <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM</a> core a <a href="/wiki/Digital_signal_processor" title="Digital signal processor">DSP</a> coprocessor is included. The native clock speed is 560 MHz. ARM rates the performance of the ARM926EJ-S at 1.1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Million_instructions_per_second" title="Million instructions per second">DMIPS</a>/MHz the performance of the Rockchip 2808 when executing ARM instructions is therefore 660 DMIPS roughly 26% the speed of Apple's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A4_processor" title="A4 processor">A4 processor</a>. The DSP coprocessor can support the real-time decoding of 720p video files at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitrate" title="Bitrate">bitrates</a> of up to 2.5 Mbit/s. This chip was the core of many <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">Windows Mobile</a>-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_internet_device" title="Mobile internet device">mobile internet devices</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARM9" title="ARM9">ARM9</a> core + DSP clocked at up to 560 MHz</li>
<li>Wi-Fi, 3G, GPS<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accelerometer" title="Accelerometer">Accelerometer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Secure_Digital" title="Secure Digital">SD/SDHC</a>/<a href="/wiki/MultiMediaCard" title="MultiMediaCard">MMC</a></li>
<li>Up to 800×600 display support</li>
<li>DDR and DDR2 RAM support, up to 1 GB</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RTOS" title="RTOS">RTOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK2816</b> was targeted at <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">PMP</a> devices, and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Internet_device" title="Mobile Internet device">MIDs</a>. It has the same specifications as the RK2806 but also includes HDMI output, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Android_os" title="Android os">Android</a> support, and up to 720p hardware video acceleration..</p>
<p>The <b>RK2818</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> was targeted at <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Internet_device" title="Mobile Internet device">MID</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-book_reader" title="E-book reader">E-reader</a> devices. As of 2013, it was targeted at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-book_reader" title="E-book reader">E-readers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARM9" title="ARM9">ARM9</a> core + DSP clocked at up to 640 MHz</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/USB" title="USB">USB</a> connection to Wi-Fi/Bluetooth chip</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accelerometer" title="Accelerometer">Accelerometer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Secure_Digital" title="Secure Digital">SD/SDHC</a>/<a href="/wiki/MultiMediaCard" title="MultiMediaCard">MMC</a></li>
<li>Up to 1024×768 display support</li>
<li>DDR and DDR2 RAM support, up to 4 GB</li>
<li>Up to 720p hardware video acceleration for H.264</li>
<li>Arteris FlexNoc interconnect technology</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RTOS" title="RTOS">RTOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK29xx_series">RK29xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: RK29xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Rockchip RK291x is a family of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System-on-a-chip" title="System-on-a-chip">SoCs</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A8" title="ARM Cortex-A8">ARM Cortex-A8</a> CPU core. They were presented for the first time at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronic_Show" title="Consumer Electronic Show">CES</a> 2011. The RK292x are single core SoCs based on <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a> and were first introduced in 2012.</p>
<p>The <b>RK2918</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK2918_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK2918-23">[23]</a></sup> was the first chip to decode Google <a href="/wiki/WebM" title="WebM">WebM</a> VP8 in hardware. It uses a dynamically configurable companion core to process various codecs. It encodes and decodes <a href="/wiki/H.264/MPEG-4_AVC" title="H.264/MPEG-4 AVC">H.264</a> at 1080p, and can decode many standard video formats including Xvid, H.263, AVS, MPEG4, RV, and WMV. It includes a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vivante" title="Vivante">Vivante</a> GC800 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU">GPU</a> that is compatible with <a href="/wiki/OpenGL" title="OpenGL">OpenGL</a> ES 2.0 and <a href="/wiki/OpenVG" title="OpenVG">OpenVG</a>. The RK2918 is compatible with <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> Froyo (2.2), Gingerbread (2.3), HoneyComb (3.x) and Ice Cream Sandwich (4.0).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Unofficial support for Ubuntu and other Linux flavours exists. As of 2013, it was targeted at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-book_reader" title="E-book reader">E-readers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>ARM Cortex-A8 processor, clocked at up to 1.2 GHz (due to stability reasons often limited to 1 GHz)</li>
<li>512 KB L2 cache</li>
<li>NEON <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARM_NEON" title="ARM NEON">SIMD</a> support</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vivante" title="Vivante">Vivante</a> GC800 GPU at 575 MHz supporting Open GL ES 2.0 and Open VG 1.1 support<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPU_GFLOPS_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPU_GFLOPS-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>VPU (Video Processing Unit) supporting 1080p image and video decoding for H.264, Xvid, H.263, AVS, MPEG4, RV, and WMV</li>
<li>DDR, DDR2, DDR3 RAM support</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> 1.2 Interface<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>USB 1.1 Host, USB 2.0 Host and USB 2.0 Device Interface</li>
<li>SD/MMC Interface</li>
<li>Adobe Flash Player 10.1</li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK2906</b> is basically a cost-reduced version of the RK2918, also targeted at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-book_reader" title="E-book reader">E-readers</a> as of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rockchip <b>RK2926</b> and <b>RK2928</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK292X_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK292X-26">[26]</a></sup> feature a single core <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex_A9" title="ARM Cortex A9">ARM Cortex A9</a> running at a speed up to 1.0 GHz. It replaces the Vivante GC800 GPU of the older RK291x series with an <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM</a> <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400</a> GPU. As of 2013, the RK2926 was targeted at tablets, while the RK2928 was targeted at tablets and Android TV dongles and boxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Single core <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex_A9" title="ARM Cortex A9">ARM Cortex A9</a> clocked up to 1.0 GHz</li>
<li>128 KB L2 cache<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>55 nm low power process</li>
<li>ARM <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400</a> GPU (single core, up to 330 MHz)</li>
<li>1080P multi format video decoding</li>
<li>1080P video encoding for H.264</li>
<li>Embedded <a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> 1.4b transmitter, <a href="/wiki/Audio_codec" title="Audio codec">audio codec</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">GPS</a> baseband</li>
<li>Embedded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LVDS" title="LVDS">LVDS</a> transmitter</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK30xx_series">RK30xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: RK30xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>RK3066</b> is a high performance dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a> mobile processor similar to the Samsung Exynos 4 Dual Core chip. In terms of performance, the RK3066 is between the Samsung Exynos 4210 and the Samsung Exynos 4212.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> As of 2013, it was targeted at tablets and Android TV dongles and boxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup> It has been a popular choice for both tablets and other devices since 2012.</p>
<ul>
<li>40 nm process</li>
<li>Dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a> processor (ARMv7 architecture) clocked up to 1.6 GHz</li>
<li>512 KB L2 cache<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>NEON <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARM_NEON" title="ARM NEON">SIMD</a> support</li>
<li>Quad core <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU">GPU</a>, clocked at 250 MHz supporting OpenGL ES 2.0, OpenVG 1.1 support, 9 G<a href="/wiki/FLOPS" title="FLOPS">FLOPS</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPU_GFLOPS_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-GPU_GFLOPS-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>VPU (Video Processing Unit) multimedia processor supporting 1080p image and video decoding</li>
<li>DDR, DDR2, DDR3 support, up to 2 GB</li>
<li>HDMI 1.4 interface</li>
<li>2-channels TFT LCD Interface with 5 layers and 3D display (1920×1080 maximum display Size)</li>
<li>USB 2.0 interface</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Secure_Digital" title="Secure Digital">SD</a>/<a href="/wiki/MultiMediaCard" title="MultiMediaCard">MMC</a> interface</li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK3068</b> is a version of the RK3066 specifically targeted at Android TV dongles and boxes. Its package is much smaller than the RK3066.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-7"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b>RK3028</b> is a low-cost dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a>-based processor clocked at 1.0 GHz with <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">ARM Mali-400</a> GPU. It is pin-compatible with the RK2928. It is used in a few kids tablets and low-cost Android HDMI TV dongles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b>RK3026</b> is an updated ultra-low-end dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a>-based tablet processor clocked at 1.0 GHz with <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">ARM Mali-400 MP2</a> GPU. Manufactured at 40 nm, it is pin-compatible with the RK2926. It features 1080p H.264 video encoding and 1080p decoding in multiple formats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Supporting Android 4.4,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> it has been adopted for low-end tablets in 2014.</p>
<p>The <b>RK3036</b> is a low-cost dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A7" title="ARM Cortex-A7">ARM Cortex-A7</a>-based processor released in Q4 2014 for smart set-top boxes with support for H.265 video decoding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip_RK3036_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip_RK3036-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK31xx_series">RK31xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: RK31xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>RK3188</b> was the first product in the RK31xx series, announced for production in the 2nd quarter of 2013. The RK3188 features a quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a> clocked up to 1.6 GHz frequency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup> It is targeted at tablets and Android TV dongles and boxes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-8"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup> and has been a popular choice for both tablets and other devices requiring good performance.</p>
<ul>
<li>28 nm HKMG process<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GlobalFoundries_press_release_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalFoundries_press_release-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a>, up to 1.6 GHz</li>
<li>512 KB L2 cache<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-9"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400 MP4</a> GPU, up to 600 MHz (typically 533 MHz) supporting OpenGL ES 1.1/2.0, Open G 1.1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPU_GFLOPS_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-GPU_GFLOPS-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>High performance dedicated 2D processor<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>DDR3, DDR3L, LPDDR2 support<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>Dual-panel display up to 2048x1536 resolution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3188_37-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3188-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK3188T</b> is a lower-clocked version of the RK3188, with the CPU cores running at a maximum speed of 1.4 GHz instead of 1.6 GHz. The Mali-400MP4 GPU is also clocked at a lower speed. As of early 2014, many devices advertised as using a RK3188 with a maximum clock speed of 1.6 GHz actually have a RK3188T with clock speed limited to 1.4 GHz. Operating system ROMs specifically made for the RK3188 may not work correctly with a RK3188T.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RK3188T_article_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-RK3188T_article-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b>RK3168</b>, first shown in April 2013, is a dual-core Cortex A9-based CPU, also manufactured using the 28 nm process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup> It is targeted at low-end tablets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-10"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup> The chip has seen only limited use as of May 2014.</p>
<ul>
<li>28 nm HKMG process<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GlobalFoundries_press_release_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalFoundries_press_release-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Dual-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a>, up to 1.2/1.5 GHz<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>256 KB L2 cache<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-11"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PowerVR" title="PowerVR">PowerVR SGX54x</a> GPU (originally listed as SGX540<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison_22-12"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_Rockchip_SoCs_comparison-22">[22]</a></sup>), up to 600 MHz (typically 500 MHz) GPU, supporting OpenGL ES 1.1/2.0, OpenVG 1.1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPU_GFLOPS_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-GPU_GFLOPS-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>High performance dedicated 2D processor<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>1080p multi format video decoding<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>1080p video encoding for H.264<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>DDR3, DDR3L, LPDDR2 support<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-7"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>Dual-panel display up to 1920x1080 resolution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip:_RK3168_41-8"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip:_RK3168-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK3126</b> is an entry-level tablet processor introduced in Q4 2014. Manufactured using a 40 nm process, it features a quad-core Cortex-A7 CPU up to 1.3 GHz and a Mali-400 MP2 GPU. It is pin-compatible with RK3026 and RK2926.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip_RK3126_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip_RK3126-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>40 nm process</li>
<li>Quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A7" title="ARM Cortex-A7">ARM Cortex-A7</a>, up to 1.3 GHz</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400 MP2</a> GPU</li>
<li>High performance dedicated 2D processor</li>
<li>DDR3, DDR3L memory interface</li>
<li>1080p multi-format video decoding and 1080p video encoding for H.264</li>
</ul>
<p>The <b>RK3128</b> is a higher-end variant of RK3126, also to be introduced in Q4 2014, that features more integrated external interfaces, including CVBS, HDMI, Ethernet MAC, S/PDIF, Audio DAC, and USB. It targets more fully featured tablets and set-top boxes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockchip_RK3128_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockchip_RK3128-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK32xx_series">RK32xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: RK32xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rockchip has announced the <a href="/wiki/Rockchip_RK3288" title="Rockchip RK3288">RK3288</a> for production in the second quarter of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RK3288_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-RK3288-44">[44]</a></sup> Recent information suggests that the chip uses a quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A17" title="ARM Cortex-A17">ARM Cortex-A17</a> CPU, although technically ARM Cortex-A12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UyeSee_TV_BOX_review_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-UyeSee_TV_BOX_review-45">[45]</a></sup> which as of October 1, 2014, ARM has decided to also refer to as Cortex-A17 because the latest production version of Cortex-A12 performs at a similar performance level as Cortex-A17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARM_Cortex-A12_update_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARM_Cortex-A12_update-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>28 nm HKMG process.</li>
<li>Quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A17" title="ARM Cortex-A17">ARM Cortex-A17</a>, up to 1.8 GHz</li>
<li>Quad-core ARM Mali-T760 MP4 (also called Mali-T764) GPU clocked at 600 MHz<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPU_GFLOPS_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-GPU_GFLOPS-25">[25]</a></sup> supporting <a href="/wiki/OpenGL_ES" title="OpenGL ES">OpenGL ES</a> 1.1/2.0/3.0/3.1, <a href="/wiki/OpenCL" title="OpenCL">OpenCL</a> 1.1, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renderscript" title="Renderscript">Renderscript</a>, <a href="/wiki/Direct3D" title="Direct3D">Direct3D</a> 11.1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>High performance dedicated 2D processor</li>
<li>1080P video encoding for H.264 and VP8, <a href="/wiki/Multiview_Video_Coding" title="Multiview Video Coding">MVC</a></li>
<li>4K H.264 and 10 bits <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.265" title="H.265">H.265</a> video decode, 1080p multi-video decode</li>
<li>Supports 4Kx2K H.265 resolution</li>
<li>Dual-channel DDR3, DDR3L, LPDDR2, LPDDR3</li>
<li>Up to 3840x2160 display output, <a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> 2.0</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inconsistent_information_about_CPU_cores_used_in_RK3288">Inconsistent information about CPU cores used in RK3288</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Inconsistent information about CPU cores used in RK3288">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Early reports including Rockchip first suggested in summer 2013 that the RK3288 was originally designed using a quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A12" title="ARM Cortex-A12">ARM Cortex-A12</a> configuration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Rockchip's primary foundry partner <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a> announced a partnership with ARM to optimize the ARM Cortex-A12 for their 28 nm-SLP process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> This is the same process used for earlier Rockchip chips such as the RK3188, and matches the choice of Cortex-A12 cores in the design of the RK3288.</p>
<p>In January 2014, official marketing materials listed the CPU cores as <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A17" title="ARM Cortex-A17">ARM Cortex-A17</a>. At the CES electronics show in January 2014, someone apparently corrected the CPU specification as being <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A12" title="ARM Cortex-A12">ARM Cortex-A12</a> instead of Cortex-A17 on one of the panels of their show booth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoft_CES_article_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoft_CES_article-50">[50]</a></sup> However, since then, official specifications from Rockchip's website and marketing materials as well specifications used by device manufacturers have continued to describe the CPU as a quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A17" title="ARM Cortex-A17">ARM Cortex-A17</a>.</p>
<p>Recent testing of early RK3288-based TV boxes (August/September 2014) provided evidence that the RK3288 technically contains Cortex-A12 cores, since the "<i>ARM 0xc0d</i>" CPU archtitecture reported by CPU-Z for Android is the reference for Cortex-A12, while the original Cortex-A17 is referred to as "<i>ARM 0xc0e</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UyeSee_TV_BOX_review_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-UyeSee_TV_BOX_review-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, on the ARM community website, ARM clarified the situation on October 1, 2014, saying that Cortex-A12, for which Rockchip is one of the few known customers, will be called Cortex-A17 from now on, and that all references to Cortex-A12 have been removed from ARM's website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARM_Cortex-A12_update_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARM_Cortex-A12_update-46">[46]</a></sup> ARM explained that the latest production revision of Cortex-A12 now performs close to the level of Cortex-A17 because the improvements of the Cortex-A17 now also have been applied to the latest version of Cortex-A12. In this way, Rockchip now gets the official blessing from ARM for listing the cores inside the RK3288 as Cortex-A17.</p>
<p>The first Android TV stick based on RK3288 was launched in November 2014 ("ZERO Devices Z5C Thinko"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_solution_based_on_RK3288">The solution based on RK3288</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The solution based on RK3288">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a class="external text" href="http://www.armdesigner.com/EM3288_SBC/" rel="nofollow">EM3288</a> is a single board computer based on the Rockchip RK3288, it features powerful graphics processing and video decoding ability.</p>
<p><a class="external text" href="https://forum.mqmaker.com/t/announcing-miqi-a-credit-card-sized-computer/371" rel="nofollow">MiQi SBC</a> is a single board computer in a metal case, with HDMI output, Gigabit Ethernet and 4xUSB 2.0 ports</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RK33xx_series">RK33xx series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: RK33xx series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rockchip announced the first member of the RK33xx family at the CES show in January 2015. The RK3368 is a SoC targeting tablets and media boxes featuring a 64-bit octa-core Cortex-A53 CPU and an OpenGL ES 3.1-class GPU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNXSoftware_RK3368_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNXSoftware_RK3368-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>64bits Octa-Core Cortex-A53, up to 1.5GHz</li>
<li>High-performance <a href="/wiki/PowerVR#Series_6XE_2" title="PowerVR">PowerVR SGX6110</a> GPU with support for OpenGL 3.1 and OpenGL ES 3.0</li>
<li>4Kx2K H.264/H.265 real-time video playback</li>
<li>HDMI 2.0 with 4Kx2K @ 60 fps display output</li>
</ul>
<p>The RK3399 announced by ARM at Mobile World Congress in February 2016, features six 64 bit CPUs, including 2 <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A72" title="ARM Cortex-A72">Cortex-A72</a> and 4 Cortex-A53.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Rockchip_SoC">List of Rockchip SoC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rockchip&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: List of Rockchip SoC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
